     <main class="content" itemprop="mainContentOfPage" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Blog" role="main">
      <article class="post-4962 post type-post status-publish format-standard category-make-money-blogging category-small-business-blogging category-website-blog-tips entry" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
       <header class="entry-header">
        <h1 class="entry-title" itemprop="headline">
         How to Get Serious About Blogging
        </h1>
        <p class="entry-meta">
         <time class="entry-time" datetime="2014-05-17T13:22:34+00:00" itemprop="datePublished">
          May 17, 2014
         </time>
         by
         <span class="entry-author" itemprop="author" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
          <a class="entry-author-link" href="http://byregina.com/author/scoobydoobydoo/" itemprop="url" rel="author">
           <span class="entry-author-name" itemprop="name">
            regina
           </span>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="entry-comments-link">
          <a href="http://byregina.com/serious-blogging/#comments">
           195 Comments
          </a>
         </span>
        </p>
       </header>
       <div class="entry-content" itemprop="text">
        <input class="jpibfi" type="hidden"/>
        <p>
         <img alt="What to Do When You're Ready to Get Serious About Blogging" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-6704" height="981" src="http://byregina.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/Ready-to-Get-Serious.jpg" width="708"/>
         <br/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         1. Think long &amp; hard about your blog categories.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Your categories are the main sections or magazine columns that you feature on your blog. They should appeal to your target audience. They should be logical for you. You should like talking about them.
        </p>
        <h3>
         2. Design your site to be appealing and easy on the eyes, for long amounts of time.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Oh, and yeah, I had a sweet male reader let me know that he loved reading even though I mainly use pictures of women in my posts. But, I dont want you guys to feel left out, so I made some secondary images you can feel free to pin to your boards. I mean, this is probably not what you meant, but I sure like these:
         <br/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt="Are you ready to get sexy, I mean serious, about blogging?" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-5296" height="465" src="http://byregina.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/Read-to-Get-Serious-Man1.jpg" width="335"/>
         <img alt="Are you ready to get sexy, I mean serious, about blogging?" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-5297" height="465" src="http://byregina.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/Ready-to-Get-Serious-Man2.jpg" width="335"/>
        </p>
        <h3>
         3. Be Ugly Betty.
        </h3>
        <p>
         And by that, I of course mean: pretend youre an actual magazine publisher and plan out each piece well, invest time into each piece, edit and format your posts, add great designs to your posts, write in a natural tone your readers will be drawn to, and publish regularly. If your favorite magazine missed a few issues, youd eventually find a replacement. If you arent blogging regularly, your readers might find some replacements. HarshTruthsAboutBloggingLife.com
         <br/>
         <span id="more-4962">
         </span>
        </p>
        <h3>
         4. Share each post into infinity. Also, beyond infinity.
        </h3>
        <p>
         You write and publish something once, but whos to say you cant share that post once per month on Twitter, or twice a year on Facebook, or every other month on Google+, or on multiple boards on Pinterest (spread these pins out for maximum effect). Due to the timeline nature or most social media platforms, if you only share something once, it will only be seen by a smaller than small percent of your followers. So, if your content will still be relevant in a month/year, take some time to schedule out multiple posts using a service like
         <a href="http://bufferapp.com" target="_blank" title="Buffer">
          Buffer
         </a>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         5. Make sure you know who youre talking to.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Want a free guide on how to do that? I wrote a
         <a href="http://byregina.com/ideal-reader-profile/" target="_blank" title="Who are you talking to? (How to Create an Ideal Reader Profile for Your Blog)">
          little post
         </a>
         with an ideal reader survey for you.
        </p>
        <h3>
         6. Make sure you know what those people want and need.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Your readers/clients have specific questions, desires, and needs. You can start to figure out these needs by the ideal reader survey above, by asking people, by paying attention to their comments and social media interactions, and by putting yourself in their shoes. What did you want to know when you were first starting out? What tools can make things simpler for your fans and customers? Use
         <a href="http://byregina.com/how-to-stay-consistent-with-marketing/" target="_blank" title="How to Stay Consistent with Marketing and Stay on Your Customers Mind">
          the free worksheet in this post
         </a>
         to begin to plan out posts and products that fit your readers needs.
        </p>
        <h3>
         7. Make an actual blog business plan.
        </h3>
        <p>
         What major, important things in your life do you do without planning? Your wedding? Nope. A business? Nope. Saving for a house? Probably not. Yet the stars are supposed to align for our blogs, without planning, without thought to its setup, purpose, audience, or uses.
         <a href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=c%27mon%20son" target="_blank" title="definition of C'mon Son">
          Cmon Son!
         </a>
         I highly recommend making a blog business plan. Heres
         <a href="http://byregina.com/blog-business-plan/" target="_blank" title="How to Write a Blog Business Plan (the guide for champions)">
          a template and instructions
         </a>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         8. Find 3  5 sites to follow for blogging tips, 5  10 sites in your niche to follow, and 3  5 sites not in your industry to follow for inspiration.
        </h3>
        <h3>
         9. Post frequently + consistently, with quality as your best friend.
        </h3>
        <p>
         I mean, actually frequently. Once a month is for the birds. Theres no magical formula, but most pro bloggers agree that at least once per week is necessary. As you get to know your readers better, youll begin to understand what they want, need, and expect. Try to cater to them while maintaining your brand goals and sanity.
        </p>
        <h3>
         10. Invest in your blog.
        </h3>
        <p>
         The things you spend money on are the things you want to get value out of. The things you spend money on are the important things that you care about. The best things in life are free, but some of the things that help you create your best life cost (a smidgen of) $$. 
         <a href="http://ctt.ec/3aP1f">
          Tweet that one
         </a>
         for me. It might not even make sense, but just go with it. It feels right.
        </p>
        <p>
         Some small investments you can make: logo and header design (Im investing in this right nowcoming soon), blog design, software to make your life easier, books on blogging, a sweet home office setup, and premium coffee to help you think. That last one is legit, right?
        </p>
        <h3>
         11. Format your posts to be read by busy, lazy humans.
        </h3>
        <p>
         You know, things like numbered lists, bullet points, bold titles or headings (when necessary). Youre smart. You feel me on this one.
        </p>
        <h3>
         12. Create a content calendar.
        </h3>
        <p>
         I used to use a planner that simply included suggested post dates and categories (colorful picture below) and the
         <a href="https://wordpress.org/plugins/editorial-calendar/" target="_blank" title="Editorial Calendar">
          Editorial Calendar
         </a>
         WordPress plugin (picture below) because I like a visual representation of when I should post. Now I use my
         <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0988780070/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0988780070&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=cyrec-20&amp;linkId=TETRANP3KW4ZE7WM" target="_blank" title="EPIC BLOG Planner">
          EPIC BLOG: One-year Editorial Planner + Workbook
         </a>
         (below). Whatever you use, make some type of content plan.
        </p>
        <p>
         Without a plan, youll get around to that one post about that one thing on the 10th of NeverEver.
         <br/>
         <br/>
         <img alt="organizing your blog schedule: byRegina content calendar" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-4966" height="178" src="http://byregina.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/Content-Calendar.jpg" width="335"/>
         <img alt="WordPress Editorial Calendar Plugin" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-4965" height="178" src="http://byregina.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/WP-EditorialCalendar.jpg" width="335"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0988780070/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0988780070&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=cyrec-20&amp;linkId=TETRANP3KW4ZE7WM">
          <img alt="EPIC BLOG Editorial Planner" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-5944" height="472" src="http://byregina.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/EPIC-BLOG.jpg" width="708"/>
         </a>
        </p>
        <h3>
         13. Now that youve created a content calendar, add in promotion &amp; maintenance tasks.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Like what Regina, what promotion and maintenance tasks? Im glad you asked friend. Try the ones on
         <a href="http://byregina.com/daily-tasks-for-bloggers-checklists/" target="_blank" title="Daily, Weekly + Monthly Business Tasks for Bloggers (free checklists my friends)">
          my free checklists
         </a>
         as a starting place. Add or cross off whatever you need to.
        </p>
        <h3>
         14. Establish a writing routine that gives you time to think.
        </h3>
        <p>
         A post may seem epic when you first plan it, and most likely it is, but I always recommend outlining, then writing, then editing and publishing, at separate times. Youll likely think of ways to add more value, and often times youll think of whole new posts that are necessary before the one youre planning in the moment. Just trust me on that one if it hasnt happened to you yet.
        </p>
        <h3>
         15. Find a blog buddy. Or five. Five is fine too.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Here are some
         <a href="http://byregina.com/find-your-bbfs/" target="_blank" title="7 Tips for Finding Your BBFs (and why you need them)">
          tips for finding your BBFs
         </a>
         (best blog friends). Ive made like 28 since writing that post, and I love you allyou know Im talking about you Erika, Naomi, Maru, Jon, Gweb and Bunny. Okay, so Ive only made six. Whatever. Whos counting?
        </p>
        <h3>
         16. Get better images . . . probably.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Or at least, get more pinnable/shareable images.
        </p>
        <h3>
         17. Learn some basic coding . . . super basic . . . dont freak out.
        </h3>
        <p>
         It will help you in so many places the blog stylist killed it with
         <a href="http://theblogstylist.com/cheat/html/" target="_blank" title="HTML Cheat Sheet">
          her HTML cheat sheet
         </a>
         for you.
        </p>
        <h3>
         18. Let people know how to help you.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Non-bloggers wont understand what the heck youre doing, and they wont necessarily know what SEO is, or how they can help yours, so, inform your friends who want to help what actually constitutes as help.
        </p>
        <h3>
         19. Be you. We wont like you if youre being someone else.
        </h3>
        <p>
         I once made a quote about that. Okay, you got me. Oscar Wilde said it and I simply made it into a pin. Semantics, my friends. Semantics. But below is the board on which you can find my (and Oscars) quote.
         <br/>
         <br/>
         <a data-pin-do="embedBoard" href="http://www.pinterest.com/byReginaTV/quotes-+-words-to-live-by/">
          Follow byRegina (blogging // business // design)s board Quotes + Words to Live By on Pinterest.
         </a>
         <br/>
         <!-- Please call pinit.js only once per page -->
         <br/>
         <script async="" src="//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js" type="text/javascript">
         </script>
        </p>
        <h3>
         20. Get a good SEO plugin/tutorial and learn how to optimize your site, posts, and images.
        </h3>
        <p>
         If youre using WordPress, I recommend
         <a href="http://byregina.com/wordpress-plugins-for-pro-bloggers/" target="_blank" title="11 Essential WordPress Plugins for Pro Bloggers (that are free and simple)">
          SEO by Yoast, along with these other plugins
         </a>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         21. If you plan to monetize your blog, start preparing for it now.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Gee how I wish there was a post about 10 non-icky
         <a href="http://byregina.com/make-money-blogging/" target="_blank" title="10 Non-icky Ways to Make Money Blogging">
          ways to monetize your blog
         </a>
         that could help you.
         <a href="http://byregina.com/make-money-blogging/" target="_blank" title="10 Non-icky Ways to Make Money Blogging">
          But I know of no such post
         </a>
         .
        </p>
        <h3>
         22. Remember social media is whack and utterly useless for bloggers.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Oh man, I crack myself up. Just checking to make sure youre still paying attention. Theres so much great stuff out there on social media. Ill simply leave you with my Pinterest board to start discovering some resources:
         <br/>
         <br/>
         <a data-pin-do="embedBoard" href="http://www.pinterest.com/byReginaTV/social-media-for-champs/">
          Follow byRegina (blogging // business // design)s board Social Media for Champs on Pinterest.
         </a>
         <br/>
         <!-- Please call pinit.js only once per page -->
         <br/>
         <script async="" src="//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js" type="text/javascript">
         </script>
        </p>
        <h3>
         23. Get high quality photos of yourself, yesterday.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Dont simply crop yourself out of your picture with seven friends, champagne glasses raised in a toast, in a dark-ish restaurant. I cant stomach any more of those pics as your professional headshot. Dont do it to me. More importantly, dont do it to you.
        </p>
        <h3>
         24. Audit your blog regularly.
        </h3>
        <p>
         That post you wrote three months ago? It totally needs a link to the post you published earlier this week because theyre heavily related and your readers will be happy to have guided/quick access to both. Always keep in mind that no matter what order you write things in, any post or page on your website has the potential to be the first post a visitor sees. P.S. Blog audits are also a great way to make sure youve included your affiliate links and product/service links in all the organic ways possible. A post on how to audit your blog is coming soon. Promise.
        </p>
        <h3>
         25. Learn some basic design skills.
        </h3>
        <p>
         You can use free software and free/inexpensive phone apps for this. You probs wont always have access to a designer who can help you on your schedule so you might as well save yourself a few dollar bills and learn to add text, filters, and decorative elements to your images. On a computer, I recommend
         <a href="http://canva.com" target="_blank" title="Canva">
          Canva
         </a>
         . On your iPhone or iPad, youll go crazy for
         <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/rhonna-designs/id667819594?mt=8&amp;uo=4&amp;at=10l8kX" target="itunes_store">
          Rhonna Designs
         </a>
         (I mean crazy!).
        </p>
        <p>
         <em>
          Yeah, I abbreviated probably to probs a few sentences back. I dont care that grownups arent supposed to abbreviate stuff, so, moving on 
         </em>
        </p>
        <h3>
         26. Double check yo self before you wreck  okay, you get it.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Grammar be your best friend. Good grammar are good for you, so if you dont be good at it, get
         <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0805088318/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0805088318&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=anjouconsu01-20&amp;linkId=WWKZXZCIRIG2QKK6" target="_blank" title="Grammar Girl's Book">
          Grammar Girls book
         </a>
         , check for spelling errors, read your posts backwards, etc. A few typos can be forgiven in the blogosphere, but a post littered with errors, that post are be hurting your credibility.
        </p>
        <h3>
         27. Be available + interactive.
        </h3>
        <p>
         No one likes a person who never responds to anything. Granted, you may be so big time that you cant get to every blog comment or tweet, but none of them? Ill accept that when you become the President of the United States, and even then, you can hire some people to help you out.
        </p>
        <h3>
         28. Pay attention to the questions your readers ask.
        </h3>
        <p>
         There may be a new blog post, new eBook you can sell, problem you can fix, or service you can offer, lingering in those questions. Also, youre showing yourself as available and interactive when you answer those questions and provide great tips.
        </p>
        <h3>
         29. Pay attention to the comments your readers leave on all channels (your blog, Facebook, Twitter, Pinterest, email).
        </h3>
        <p>
         Refer to the point above for the why.
        </p>
        <h3>
         30. Guest post like a champ.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Once you have a small to medium collection of quality content to lead people back to, pitch some sites that fit your brand (or that are frequented by your ideal readers) to do a guest post. Think about larger online magazines and websites as well. These guest posting opportunities will help you build relationships and will lead new readers back to your site.
        </p>
        <h3>
         31. Accept guest posts like a champ.
        </h3>
        <p>
         If someone else is willing to say some valuable and entertaining stuff on your blog, let them. Make sure each post fits your blog, fits your readers, and is the type of quality content you want your blog to be known for. Make sure to promote your guest authors and show them love. They will likely spread word of their guest post, which can potentially give you lots of new readers.
        </p>
        <h3>
         32. Dont neglect your business tasks.
        </h3>
        <p>
         You know, the things like accounting + filing taxes, and learning how to be awesome at business. This is where your blog business plan (#7 above) will come in handy.
        </p>
        <h3>
         33. Dont let creative flex distract you from building your #1 brand.
        </h3>
        <p>
         Im talking to you. You who allow other shiny new projects to distract you from the main one you need to focus on. You who are like me. You who need professional help because there are so many ideas racing through your head. Use
         <a href="http://byregina.com/creative-flex-is-messing-with-your-brand/" target="_blank" title="How Creative Flex is Messing with Your Brand (and 5 Steps to Fix It)">
          these steps
         </a>
         to minimize your crazy.
        </p>
        <hr/>
        <p>
         Photo of woman:  chesterF  Fotolia.com
         <br/>
         Photo of man working out:  iko  Fotolia.com
         <br/>
         Photo of man in suit:  GooDAura  Fotolia.com
        </p>

               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://byregina.com/serious-blogging/#comment-1760" itemprop="url">

            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Noor, Im with you 100%, but you have one of the best eyes for style Ive ever seen, so I cant even keep up with you. Seriously, everything you pin on Pinterest, without looking at who pinned it, Im like, Uh huh, that must be Noors pin. Everything is so beautiful . . . and lets not even talk about how great your pre-made WP themes are.
             </p>
             <p>
              It makes me wonder though, do people sometimes just not know their blog content is being presented unattractively? It would be great if we lived in a world where we didnt judge a book by its cover, but we do. And to be honest, its good business sense. I want to write a post about it. After all, we have so many things competing for our time and attention that we want to give our time to the most valuable, meaningful content. Often times, people who create great value put in the effort to present it in a beautiful way. Therefore we logically assume that if you put little to no effort into the appearance of your thing, it might not be the value we seek. Haha. Too much?
             </p>
            </div>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-1756">
         <article itemprop="comment" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/UserComments">
          <header class="comment-header">
           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="creator" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
            <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/3ceb0ce19e4f3110944fbab274a9e357?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/3ceb0ce19e4f3110944fbab274a9e357?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>
            <span itemprop="name">
             <a class="comment-author-link" href="http://www.mostpixels.com" itemprop="url" rel="external nofollow">
              Steve Faber
             </a>
            </span>
            <span class="says">
             says
            </span>
           </p>
           <p class="comment-meta">
            <time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-05-18T12:37:39+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
             <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://byregina.com/serious-blogging/#comment-1756" itemprop="url">
              May 18, 2014 at 12:37 pm
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Regina,
           </p>
           <p>
            Nice post and great ideas.
           </p>
           <p>
            1) You should also keyword research your categories, although not to the point where it favors search engines over humans
            <br/>
            2) Are you kidding??? Of COURSE your male readers enjoy a blog overflowing with images of attractive women.
           </p>
           <p>
            4) Excellent Point. Due to its transitory nature, Twitter especially rewards  re-posting, and at different times. That catches those who missed it the first time among their multitude of followers.
            <br/>
            5) The number one rule of marketing : Know your audience. Write in their language; how theyll understand and relate to it.
            <br/>
            6) Number two rule of marketing: Know what they want, what to give them, and how.
            <br/>
            7) Spot on here. Too many go into blogging as a hobby and expect theyll get rich off of it. No such luck! Its a real business, and as such, a plan is nearly vital for success.
           </p>
           <p>
            9) You cant overstate that one. Ive experienced my best blogging results posting 3 -5 times per week, but not ignoring rules 5-6 above, and keeping the quality high.
           </p>
           <p>
            12)  Want to eliminate blogger block? Follow this rule and make an editorial calendar. Youll thank  yourself for it when its been 3 days since your last post and nothings jumped into your head that seems worthwhile yet.
           </p>
           <p>
            13) You can do these on he same day, too. I used to reserve the first two hours for those, and write later in the day. Now I typically do the reverse. Some bloggers I know set aside a couple of days for promo and maintenance than create content on the others. Do what works best for you, just dont forget those are vital parts of successful blogging.
           </p>
           <p>
            15) This may be the 2nd most important point youve raised. Business (and life) is most successful when you build solid relationships. It may be even more true for blogging. It boosts creativity, promo opportunities, and reach. Its a win-win-win. You, the other bloggers, and your audience all benefit. Do it!
           </p>
           <p>
            30) See #15 above..
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-reply">
           <a aria-label="Reply to Steve Faber" class="comment-reply-link" href="/serious-blogging/?replytocom=1756#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-1756", "1756", "respond", "4962" )'>
            Reply

            <header class="comment-header">
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="creator" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/264071d121f83cf79487afbfbc087325?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/264071d121f83cf79487afbfbc087325?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>
              <span itemprop="name">
               regina
              </span>
              <span class="says">
               says
              </span>
             </p>
             <p class="comment-meta">
              <time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-05-19T13:24:24+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://byregina.com/serious-blogging/#comment-1816" itemprop="url">
                May 19, 2014 at 1:24 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Steve, if there were an award for comment that made my weekend . . . youd be winning it right now. Thank you for taking the time to read this post and to give such great feedback. I truly appreciate that.
             </p>
             <p>
              I think you bring up some good points: keyword research, attractive women making for good pics for really any audience, and many more.
             </p>
             <p>
              I think the important points are the ones you identified: (1) treating your blog as a business if you hope to make money or grow your platform and (2) building solid relationships.
             </p>
             <p>
              Im not a huge fan of the word networking the way its most often used. It implies a What can I get out of this? What can you do for me? type of attitude, and lets be honest, no one likes to go into any type of relationship thinking that theyre only there to serve your needs. Building solid relationships is based on What can I do for you? How can we work together? What can I build to help you reach your goals? How can we just enjoy each others company?
             </p>
             <p>
              Im excited to be reminded that many other people view relationship building this way. Thanks again Steve for your time. Im headed to check out your site now.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-reply">

               <p>
                Deciding factors, hmmm mostly because I feel like I am trapped in a box right now.  I see what other people can do with their online spaces but I feel like Im not allowed to play on that team or something.  Its just way too limiting.  Im hoping to constantly push towards bigger and better.
               </p>
               <p>

               </p>
               <p>
                Just have to say again I love your site.  I did your Ideal Reader Profile the other night and was so pleased with myself that I literally read it out loud to my boyfriend.  He loved this, Im sure.

Im a big fan of the work I see from Bethany of LoveGrowsDesign.com, when it comes to Genesis. ShaniceCameron.com just opened a new shop with some pretty themes as well.         <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="comment-3154">
         <article itemprop="comment" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/UserComments">
          <header class="comment-header">
           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="creator" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
            <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/4eecd5cea26d1e02b0e49aaaabec0bd4?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/4eecd5cea26d1e02b0e49aaaabec0bd4?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>
            <span itemprop="name">
             Toady
            </span>
            <span class="says">
             says
            </span>
           </p>
           <p class="comment-meta">
            <time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-06-23T20:22:48+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
             <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://byregina.com/serious-blogging/#comment-3154" itemprop="url">
              June 23, 2014 at 8:22 pm
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Im not a blogger.  I honestly havent the attention span for itSQUIRREL!however I just wanted to add, because I do a LOT of academic writing (Im working toward my MBA)
           </p>
           <p>
            Write how you are comfortable!
           </p>
           <p>
            I get the ODDEST looks because Ill be sitting on the couch, or at a softball game, or in McDonalds staring off into outer space with a pencil (usually mechanical) in hand and a notebook (you know, those things with the metal spirals on one side that go on sale at least once a year for schoolchildren?  I really need to buy stock in one of those companiesthat aside)
           </p>
           <p>
            ALL my essays, homework assignments, and even discussion posts (items I get graded on) are written out by hand with said pencil and notebook.  I just think better that way.  NO ONE understands this and my frantic search for a notebook before my last session (I RAN OUT!) had my husband rolling his eyes and begrudgingly making a special trip to town just so I could get one (isnt he sweet) at 11 at night (which is late for us!  Hes a farmer)
           </p>
           <p>
            The point is thats how I think best.  My raw ideas get scratched out on paper then by the time I sit down at the computer, between the random scratches and more thought (and usually several cups of coffee) I edit what I wrote as I type and it ends up being far more polished then if I were to just sit down to type it.  This is especially important to me in any formal writing projectand ifunlike meyou are going to be a blogger some amount of formality will go into your writing.  Sosecret notebook and pencil loversdont be ashamed.  Embrace your preferred writing method!
           </p>
           <p>
            Those of you that can sit at a computer and formulate thoughts withoutSQUIRREL!!!distractionI (seriously) applaud you and you embrace your ability not to get sucked into FB, TUMBLR, Twitter or YouTube for HOURS on end.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-reply">
           <a aria-label="Reply to Toady" class="comment-reply-link" href="/serious-blogging/?replytocom=3154#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-3154", "3154", "respond", "4962" )'>
            Reply
           </a>
          </div>

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Toady, haha. Thank you for your excellent comment. Im actually like you, often. I have notebooks that I write or outline post/products in before I type them. Writing them twice like this does provide better ideas, clarity, and wording a lot of the time.
             </p>
             <p>
              And, as you said, it can be simple to get distracted online. I try to do a first draft without Internet research, for most topics.
             </p>
             <p>
              Good luck with your MBA, and youre right, I think I need some stock in one of those notebook companies too. My own notebook buying habits keeps some of them in businessIm convinced.
             </p>
             <p>
              Thanks for taking some time to stop by the blog and read. Please, please forgive me for taking so long to respond.

               </p>
               <p>
                I am working on adding graphics, I actually thought that page was hidden, he he, I guess not  but that is a question I had, I launched my blog, and only after getting over that hurdle did the ideas really start to pour out, so Im adding pages, content, graphics that I want to enhance my site, so after launching it, its back in a work in progress stage, SO my question is, is it okay to add components piecemeal as I create it, or should I wait till its all ready and re-launch at once, or does it really matter as long I get it accomplished?!?
               </p>

              <li class="comment odd alt depth-4" id="comment-8555">
               <article itemprop="comment" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/UserComments">
                <header class="comment-header">
                 <p class="comment-author" itemprop="creator" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                  <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/264071d121f83cf79487afbfbc087325?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/264071d121f83cf79487afbfbc087325?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>
                  <span itemprop="name">
                   regina
                  </span>
                  <span class="says">
                   says
                  </span>
                 </p>
                 <p class="comment-meta">
                  <time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-09-03T23:41:00+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
                   <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://byregina.com/serious-blogging/#comment-8555" itemprop="url">
                    September 3, 2014 at 11:41 pm
                   </a>
                  </time>
                 </p>
                </header>
                <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
                 <p>
                  Frances, thats a really good question. I think there are a number of ways to look at it and it depends on your personality. Let me explain:
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  If you are someone that is motivated by seeing a live thing in need of modifications, prettying, and attention (this is me for sure), then you might want to leave it up. Seeing it up can inspire you, make you want to improve it, and still allow others to find you and interact with you in the meantime.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  However, if you think someones impression of you and your blog will be drastically different after your graphics/tweaks are added (and that they are more likely to stick around, subscribe, follow, etc.), then definitely do a hide and relaunch. You can use a WordPress plugin like Ultimate Coming Soon or Coming Soon Pro (if youre on the WordPress.org version) to hide your site while you work on it.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  I feel that as long as you get it done, it doesnt really matter too much, but, knowing your readers and yourself, perhaps judge whether one method or the other would kill motivation or turn away readers. And . . . if its only going to take a few days, Id say leave it up. A re-launch only makes sense to me if theres a real pause and build up for it.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  I hope Im making sense. Feel free to virtual slap me if not. Thanks for your comment again.
                 </p>
                </div>
                <div class="comment-reply">
                 <a aria-label="Reply to regina" class="comment-reply-link" href="/serious-blogging/?replytocom=8555#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-8555", "8555", "respond", "4962" )'>
                  Reply
                 </a>
                </div>

            Thank you for the great information. We are in the process of starting to grow our blog after our initial 3 months of trial and error; things seem to be coming along now! We have utilized the tips and advice given by your blog and it all seems to be very helpful so far!
           </p>
           <p>
            Thanks again!
            <br/>
            Falynn | OUTINON.com
           </p>
